I believe the sequel didn't introduce enough changes for a true sequel. This applies not only to the graphics but also to the gameplay. The game lacks features like dynamic weather and day-night cycles, which would greatly enhance the atmosphere. We essentially got the same game with slightly updated animations, different character skins, and the ability to fly around like Superman, defying the laws of physics. While I understand that people love Spider-Man, and this game will likely be enjoyable for fans, I can't help but feel that it missed an opportunity to deliver more substantial improvements. Rather than creating a truly new experience, they opted to add a few mechanics to the previous game. This approach works well for expansions, but not for a standalone sequel. They increased the speed of movement in the city but it doesn't necessarily make the game better. Slower flights, smoother animations, realistic physics, and a sense of inertia would have provided a more satisfying gameplay experience compared to the fast-paced web-swinging we have now. A slower pace allows players to appreciate the intricate details of the environment, while realistic physics adds authenticity. It's disappointing that the game still doesn't allow players to interact with the environment using their feet while flying. The ability to touch the ground or water with realistic splashes would have added depth to the gameplay, allowing for potential mistakes and increasing immersion. They could have even implemented a scoring system for perfectly timed R2 presses, rewarding players for skillfully maneuvering close to surfaces. Additionally, the removal of the stealth assist system and the scripted alarm activation when liberating outposts is also a letdown. These features added a layer of strategy and tension to the game, and their absence is noticeable. Of course, this is just my personal opinion. If you enjoy the game, I'm genuinely happy for you. As a longtime fan of the web-slinger, I can't help but feel a tinge of envy.
